Graph-Regularized Sparse Autoencoders for LLM Safety Steering
Authors: Jehyeok Yeon, Federico Cinus, Yifan Wu, Luca Luceri
First: 2025-12-07T04:46:30+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-15T09:56:17+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Sparse autoencoders (SAEs) are increasingly used to extract activation directions for inference-time steering, but their standard sparsity objective treats latent features as independent. This prior can be poorly matched to high-level safety behaviors, where refusal and harmful compliance appear to depend on distributed structure in activation space. We introduce Graph-Regularized Sparse Autoencoders (GSAE), a dictionary-learning method that learns safety-steering directions by smoothing SAE decoder vectors over a neuron co-activation graph and applying the resulting direction bank through a two-gate runtime controller. Empirically, GSAE improves selective refusal across JailbreakBench, HarmBench, and XSTest, increasing harmful-request refusal while keeping benign-prompt refusals low. On Llama-3-8B, replacing the standard SAE with GSAE in an otherwise identical pipeline improves $Δ_s$ by $20.1$ points on JailbreakBench and $16.8$ points on HarmBench. GSAE outperforms activation-steering baselines and black-box guardrails, preserves benign-task performance, generalizes across Llama-3, Mistral, Qwen 2.5, and Phi-4, and remains strong under black-box and gray-box jailbreak attacks.
中文标题/摘要
标题：图正则化稀疏自编码器用于大型语言模型安全引导
稀疏自编码器（SAE）越来越多地用于提取推理时引导的激活方向，但其标准稀疏性目标将潜在特征视为独立。这一先验可能与高层次的安全行为不匹配，其中拒绝和有害的顺从似乎依赖于激活空间中的分布结构。我们引入图正则化稀疏自编码器（GSAE），这是一种字典学习方法，通过在神经元共同激活图上平滑SAE解码器向量来学习安全引导方向，并通过双门运行时控制器应用结果方向库。实证结果表明，GSAE在JailbreakBench、HarmBench和XSTest上改善了选择性拒绝，增加了有害请求的拒绝，同时保持良性提示的拒绝率较低。在Llama-3-8B上，在其他条件相同的管道中用GSAE替换标准SAE，使得JailbreakBench上的$Δ_s$提高了$20.1$点，HarmBench上提高了$16.8$点。GSAE优于激活引导基线和黑箱护栏，保持良性任务性能，在Llama-3、Mistral、Qwen 2.5和Phi-4上具有良好的泛化能力，并在黑箱和灰箱越狱攻击下表现强劲。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of standard sparse autoencoders (SAEs) in safety steering for large language models (LLMs), where the independence assumption of latent features does not align well with complex safety behaviors. Previous methods have struggled with effectively managing the trade-off between harmful compliance and benign refusals. The proposed Graph-Regularized Sparse Autoencoders (GSAE) enhance the learning of safety-steering directions by incorporating a neuron co-activation graph, which allows for a more distributed representation of activation space. This method is well-motivated as it directly targets the shortcomings of existing approaches. The contribution of the paper lies in demonstrating that GSAE significantly improves selective refusal rates on various benchmarks, achieving a 20.1-point increase on JailbreakBench and a 16.8-point increase on HarmBench, while maintaining performance on benign tasks and showing robustness against different attack scenarios.

Benchmark of Benchmarks: Unpacking Influence and Code Repository Quality in LLM Safety Benchmarks
Authors: Junjie Chu, Xinyue Shen, Ye Leng, Michael Backes, Yun Shen, Yang Zhang
First: 2026-03-03T09:10:45+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-14T18:30:07+00:00
Comments: 24 pages. 19 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid expansion of research in LLM safety presents challenges in tracking advancements, making benchmarks important evaluation infrastructures for identifying key trends and facilitating systematic comparisons. Yet no systematic assessment exists of their code quality and runnability, nor of what factors are associated with the community's adoption of certain benchmarks over others. To address this gap, we conduct a systematic measurement study of 31 LLM safety benchmarks (covering prompt injection, jailbreak, and hallucination) with 382 non-benchmark papers as a control group, combining automated static analysis, human runnability testing (220+ person-hours), and bibliometric analysis. We find that only 39\% of benchmark repositories can run without modification, only 16\% provide flawless installation guides, and a mere 6\% include ethical considerations despite containing potentially harmful content. These deficiencies persist across the study period with no significant improvement. Analyzing adoption factors, we find that benchmark adoption correlates with author prominence and code runnability, but not with code quality standards such as Pylint score and maintainability, suggesting that the community's benchmark selection does not reward higher coding standards. Based on these results, we identify potential safety and reliability concerns. Some safety benchmark repositories openly expose harmful content, such as successful jailbreak responses, without any ethical warning or access control, effectively serving as unguarded attack resources. Furthermore, when benchmarks require ad-hoc modifications to run, downstream safety evaluations across different papers may not be comparable. We present case studies illustrating these concrete consequences and propose a targeted checklist to help benchmark contributors improve code quality, documentation, and ethical practices.
中文标题/摘要
标题：基准中的基准：解读LLM安全基准中的影响力和代码库质量
LLM安全研究的快速扩展带来了跟踪进展的挑战，使基准成为识别关键趋势和促进系统比较的重要评估基础设施。然而，目前尚无对其代码质量和可运行性的系统评估，也没有研究社区对某些基准的采用与其他基准之间的关联因素。为了解决这一空白，我们对31个LLM安全基准（涵盖提示注入、越狱和幻觉）进行系统测量研究，并以382篇非基准论文作为对照组，结合自动静态分析、人为可运行性测试（220+人小时）和文献计量分析。我们发现，只有39%的基准代码库可以在不修改的情况下运行，只有16%提供无瑕疵的安装指南，尽管包含潜在有害内容，但仅有6%考虑了伦理问题。这些缺陷在研究期间持续存在，没有显著改善。在分析采用因素时，我们发现基准采用与作者知名度和代码可运行性相关，但与代码质量标准（如Pylint分数和可维护性）无关，这表明社区的基准选择并未奖励更高的编码标准。基于这些结果，我们识别出潜在的安全和可靠性问题。一些安全基准代码库公开暴露有害内容，例如成功的越狱响应，而没有任何伦理警告或访问控制，实际上充当了无防护的攻击资源。此外，当基准需要临时修改才能运行时，不同论文之间的下游安全评估可能无法比较。我们展示了这些具体后果的案例研究，并提出了一份针对性的检查清单，以帮助基准贡献者提高代码质量、文档和伦理实践。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the challenges in evaluating LLM safety benchmarks due to the rapid growth in this field, highlighting the lack of systematic assessments of code quality and runnability. Previous methods did not adequately evaluate these aspects, leading to issues such as low runnability and poor documentation among benchmark repositories. The proposed approach involves a systematic measurement study of 31 LLM safety benchmarks and 382 control papers, utilizing automated static analysis, human testing, and bibliometric analysis to uncover significant deficiencies in code quality and ethical considerations. The findings reveal that a majority of benchmarks are not runnable without modifications and lack proper ethical warnings, raising safety concerns. The paper contributes by identifying factors influencing benchmark adoption and proposing a checklist aimed at enhancing code quality and ethical practices in benchmark development, ultimately supporting the goal of improving safety evaluations in LLM research.
本研究针对LLM安全基准评估中的挑战，强调了对代码质量和可运行性缺乏系统评估的问题。以往的方法未能充分评估这些方面，导致基准库的可运行性低和文档质量差。所提出的方法包括对31个LLM安全基准的系统测量研究，采用自动静态分析、人为可运行性测试和文献计量分析，揭示了代码质量和伦理考虑的缺陷。研究结果显示，显著比例的基准无法在不修改的情况下运行，且缺乏适当的安装指南，这引发了对安全性和可靠性的担忧。本文的贡献在于识别影响基准采用的因素，并提出一份清单，旨在改善基准贡献中的代码质量和伦理实践，最终支持提升LLM安全评估的目标。
The Great Pretender: A Stochasticity Problem in LLM Jailbreak
Authors: Jean-Philippe Monteuuis, Cong Chen, Jonathan Petit
First: 2026-05-14T06:05:37+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-14T06:05:37+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
"Oh-Oh, yes, I'm the great pretender. Pretending that I'm doing well. My need is such, I pretend too much..." summarizes the state in the area of jailbreak creation and evaluation. You find this method to generate adversarial attacks proposed by a reputable institution (e.g., BoN from Anthropic or Crescendo from Microsoft Research). However, this method does not deliver on the promise claimed in the paper despite having top ASR scores against industry-grade LLMs. You successfully generate the jailbreak prompts against your target (open) model. However, the generated jailbreak prompt works against the target model with a 50% consecutive success rate (5 out of 10 attempts) despite having an 80% ASR (on paper) on the latest closed-source model (with a guardrail system)! This observation leads us to think. First, Attack Success Rate (ASR), the primary metric for LLM jailbreak benchmarking, is not a stable quantity. Second, published ASR numbers are therefore systematically inflated and incomparable across papers. Therefore, we wonder "Why a successful jailbreak prompt does not perform consistently well against a target model on which the prompts have been optimized?". To answer this question, we study the impact of stochasticity not only during attack evaluation but also during attack generation. Our evaluation includes several jailbreak attacks, models (different sizes and providers), and judges. In addition, we propose a new metric and two new frameworks (CAS-eval and CAS-gen). Our evaluation framework, CAS-eval, shows that an attack can have an ASR drop of up to 30 percentage points when a jailbreak prompt needs to succeed on more than one attempt. Thankfully, our attack generation framework (CAS-gen) improves previous jailbreak methods and helps them recover this loss of 30 percentage points!
中文标题/摘要
标题：伟大的伪装者：LLM越狱中的随机性问题
"哦-哦，是的，我是伟大的伪装者。假装我做得很好。我的需求如此，我假装得太多……"总结了越狱创建和评估领域的现状。你发现了由一个知名机构（例如，Anthropic的BoN或微软研究院的Crescendo）提出的生成对抗攻击的方法。然而，尽管在行业级LLM上具有顶级的ASR分数，这种方法并没有兑现论文中所声称的承诺。你成功地针对目标（开放）模型生成了越狱提示。然而，生成的越狱提示在目标模型上的连续成功率为50%（10次尝试中有5次成功），尽管在最新的闭源模型（带有护栏系统）上在纸面上有80%的ASR！这一观察促使我们思考。首先，攻击成功率（ASR），作为LLM越狱基准测试的主要指标，并不是一个稳定的量。其次，发布的ASR数字因此系统性地被夸大，并且在不同论文之间不可比。因此，我们想知道“为什么成功的越狱提示在经过优化的目标模型上表现不一致？”为了回答这个问题，我们研究了随机性在攻击评估和攻击生成中的影响。我们的评估包括几种越狱攻击、模型（不同大小和提供者）和评审。此外，我们提出了一个新指标和两个新框架（CAS-eval和CAS-gen）。我们的评估框架CAS-eval显示，当越狱提示需要在多次尝试中成功时，攻击的ASR可能下降多达30个百分点。值得庆幸的是，我们的攻击生成框架（CAS-gen）改善了之前的越狱方法，并帮助它们恢复这30个百分点的损失！
Summary / 总结
This paper addresses the inconsistencies in the effectiveness of jailbreak prompts for large language models (LLMs), highlighting that existing methods, such as those from reputable institutions, often report inflated Attack Success Rates (ASR) that do not translate into reliable performance. The proposed approach introduces two new frameworks, CAS-eval for evaluating attack performance and CAS-gen for generating more effective jailbreak prompts, which together tackle the stochasticity issues observed in both attack generation and evaluation. The contribution lies in demonstrating that ASR can drop significantly when prompts are tested for consecutive success, revealing the need for more robust evaluation metrics. The methodology involves comprehensive testing across various models and attack types, ultimately showing that the new frameworks can mitigate the performance drop, achieving a more consistent success rate in jailbreak attempts, thus supporting the goal of reliable LLM jailbreak evaluation.
本文探讨了大型语言模型（LLM）越狱提示的有效性不一致性，强调现有方法虽然在理论上实现了高攻击成功率（ASR），但在实际应用中往往失败。所提出的方法通过在攻击生成和评估过程中纳入随机性分析，与以往方法不同，这些方法忽视了这一点，导致ASR指标被夸大。本文贡献了一个新的评估框架（CAS-eval）和生成框架（CAS-gen），证明在多次测试提示时，ASR可能显著下降。所提出的方法论表明，CAS-gen能够恢复高达30个百分点的ASR损失，从而提高了在各种模型和条件下越狱提示的可靠性。
Reducing the Safety Tax in LLM Safety Alignment with On-Policy Self-Distillation
Authors: Yu Fu, Longxuan Yu, Haz Sameen Shahgir, Zhipeng Wei, Hui Liu, N. Benjamin Erichson, Yue Dong
First: 2026-05-14T03:40:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-14T03:40:07+00:00
Comments: 20 pages, 5 figures
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Safety alignment often improves robustness to harmful queries at the cost of reasoning ability, a tradeoff known as the safety tax. A common cause is distributional mismatch: supervised fine-tuning trains the target model on safety demonstrations produced by humans, external models, or fixed self-generated traces, rather than on trajectories sampled from its own policy. We identify off-policy training mismatch as a second source of this tax and study on-policy self-distillation for safety alignment, which we call OPSA. The model generates its own rollouts and receives dense per-token KL supervision from a frozen teacher copy of itself conditioned on a privileged safety context. Because this teacher must be safer than the sampled student trajectory, we introduce \emph{teacher flip rate}: a criterion that measures how often a privileged context converts unsafe responses into safe ones. We use this signal to search for contexts that activate latent safety reasoning rather than merely elicit safe-looking demonstrations. Across two reasoning-model families and five model scales, OPSA achieves a stronger safety--reasoning tradeoff than off-policy self-distillation and external-teacher distillation under matched data and full-parameter fine-tuning, with the largest gains on smaller models (+8.85 points on R1-Distill-1.5B and +5.49 points on Qwen3-0.6B). The gains persist across training-set sizes and adaptive jailbreak evaluations. Token-level analyses further show that OPSA concentrates updates near early compliance-decision tokens, providing a mechanism for improving safety while preserving general reasoning.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过策略自蒸馏减少大型语言模型安全对齐中的安全税
安全对齐通常在提高对有害查询的鲁棒性的同时牺牲推理能力，这种权衡被称为安全税。一个常见原因是分布不匹配：监督微调在由人类、外部模型或固定自生成轨迹产生的安全示范上训练目标模型，而不是在其自身策略采样的轨迹上。我们将离策略训练不匹配识别为这种税的第二个来源，并研究用于安全对齐的策略自蒸馏，称为OPSA。该模型生成自己的回滚，并从一个冻结的教师副本中接收每个标记的密集KL监督，该教师副本基于特权安全上下文。由于该教师必须比采样的学生轨迹更安全，我们引入了“教师翻转率”：一个衡量特权上下文将不安全响应转化为安全响应的频率的标准。我们利用这个信号寻找激活潜在安全推理的上下文，而不仅仅是引出看似安全的示范。在两个推理模型系列和五个模型规模中，OPSA在匹配数据和全参数微调下实现了比离策略自蒸馏和外部教师蒸馏更强的安全-推理权衡，在较小模型上获得了最大的提升（R1-Distill-1.5B上提高8.85分，Qwen3-0.6B上提高5.49分）。这些提升在训练集大小和自适应越狱评估中持续存在。标记级分析进一步表明，OPSA集中更新在早期合规决策标记附近，提供了一种在保持一般推理的同时提高安全性的机制。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the challenge of safety alignment in large language models (LLMs), which often leads to a tradeoff known as the safety tax, where improved robustness to harmful queries compromises reasoning ability. Previous methods, including off-policy self-distillation and external-teacher distillation, suffer from distributional mismatches that hinder effective safety alignment. The proposed approach, on-policy self-distillation for safety alignment (OPSA), mitigates these issues by allowing the model to generate its own rollouts and receive supervision from a frozen teacher model, thereby ensuring that the teacher's responses are safer than the student's. The paper contributes a novel criterion called teacher flip rate to identify contexts that enhance safety reasoning. OPSA demonstrates superior performance in achieving a better safety-reasoning tradeoff compared to existing methods, with significant improvements observed in smaller models, achieving gains of +8.85 points on R1-Distill-1.5B and +5.49 points on Qwen3-0.6B, thus supporting the goal of enhancing safety without sacrificing reasoning capabilities.

Quantifying LLM Safety Degradation Under Repeated Attacks Using Survival Analysis
Authors: Zvi Topol
First: 2026-05-13T01:26:06+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-13T01:26:06+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) are increasingly deployed in a wide range of applications, yet remain vulnerable to adversarial jailbreak attacks that circumvent their safety guardrails. Existing evaluation frameworks typically report binary success/failure metrics, failing to capture the temporal dynamics of how attacks succeed under persistent adversarial pressure. This preliminary work proposes a novel evaluation framework that applies survival analysis techniques to characterize LLM jailbreak vuln`erability. Our approach models the time-to-jailbreak as a survival outcome, enabling estimation of hazard functions, survival curves, and risk factors associated with successful attacks. We evaluate three LLMs against a subset of prompts from the HarmBench dataset spanning three attack categories. Our analysis reveals that models exhibit distinct vulnerability profiles: while one model demonstrates rapid degradation under iterative attacks, the two other models show consistent moderate vulnerability. Our framework provides actionable insights for model and LLM application developers and establishes survival analysis as a rigorous methodology for LLM safety evaluation.
中文标题/摘要

RACC: Representation-Aware Coverage Criteria for LLM Safety Testing
Authors: Zeming Wei, Zhixin Zhang, Chengcan Wu, Yihao Zhang, Xiaokun Luan, Meng Sun
First: 2026-02-02T16:20:51+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-12T03:47:11+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) face severe safety risks from jailbreak attacks, yet current safety testing largely relies on static datasets and lacks systematic criteria to evaluate test suite quality and adequacy. While coverage criteria have proven effective for smaller neural networks, they are impractical for LLMs due to computational overhead and the entanglement of safety-critical signals with irrelevant neuron activations. To address these issues, we propose RACC (Representation-Aware Coverage Criteria), a set of coverage criteria specialized for LLM safety testing. RACC first extracts safety representations from the LLM's hidden states using a small calibration set of harmful prompts, then measures test prompts' concept activations against these directions, and finally computes coverage through six criteria assessing both individual and compositional safety concept coverage. Experiments on multiple LLMs and safety benchmarks show that RACC reliably rewards high-quality jailbreak test suites while remaining insensitive to redundant or invalid inputs, which is a key distinction that neuron-level criteria fail to make. We further demonstrate RACC's practical value in two applications, including test suite prioritization and attack prompt sampling, and validate its generalization across diverse settings and configurations. Overall, RACC provides a scalable and principled foundation for coverage-guided LLM safety testing.
中文标题/摘要
标题：RACC：面向表示的LLM安全测试覆盖标准
大型语言模型（LLM）面临来自越狱攻击的严重安全风险，但当前的安全测试主要依赖静态数据集，缺乏系统性标准来评估测试套件的质量和充分性。虽然覆盖标准在较小的神经网络中已被证明有效，但由于计算开销和安全关键信号与无关神经元激活的纠缠，它们在LLM中不切实际。为了解决这些问题，我们提出了RACC（面向表示的覆盖标准），这是一组专门针对LLM安全测试的覆盖标准。RACC首先使用一小组有害提示从LLM的隐藏状态中提取安全表示，然后根据这些方向测量测试提示的概念激活，最后通过六个标准计算覆盖，评估个体和组合安全概念的覆盖。对多个LLM和安全基准的实验表明，RACC可靠地奖励高质量的越狱测试套件，同时对冗余或无效输入保持不敏感，这是神经元级标准无法做到的关键区别。我们进一步展示了RACC在两个应用中的实际价值，包括测试套件优先级排序和攻击提示采样，并验证了其在不同设置和配置中的泛化能力。总体而言，RACC为覆盖引导的LLM安全测试提供了可扩展和原则性的基础。

FragBench: Cross-Session Attacks Hidden in Benign-Looking Fragments
Authors: Astha Mehta, Niruthiha Selvanayagam, Cedric Lam, Hengxu Li, Phuc-Nguyen Nguyen, Raymond Lee, Olivia McGoffin, My, Luong, Arthur Collé, Jamie Johnson, David Williams-King, Linh Le
First: 2026-05-10T21:06:48+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-10T21:06:48+00:00
Comments: preprint of submission
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
An attacker can split a malicious goal into sub-prompts that each look benign on their own and only become harmful in combination. Existing LLM safety benchmarks evaluate prompts one at a time, or across turns of a single chat, and so do not look for a malicious signal spread across separate sessions with no shared context. We build FragBench, a benchmark drawn from 24 real-world cyber-incident campaigns, which keeps the full attack trail: the multi-fragment kill chain, the per-fragment safety-judge verdicts, sandboxed execution traces, and a matched set of benign cover sessions. FragBench splits this trail into two paired tasks: an adversarial rewriter that hardens fragments against a single-turn safety judge (FragBench Attack), and a graph-based user-level detector trained on the resulting interactions (FragBench Defense). The single-turn judge is near chance on the released corpus by construction, but four GNN variants and three classical-ML baselines all recover the cross-session feature, reaching aggregate event-level F1 = 0.88-0.96. Defending against fragmented LLM misuse therefore requires modeling the cross-session interaction graph, rather than isolated prompts. Our generator, rewriter, sandbox harness, and detector are released at https://github.com/LidaSafety/fragbench.
中文标题/摘要
标题：FragBench：隐藏在看似良性片段中的跨会话攻击
攻击者可以将恶意目标拆分为看似良性的子提示，这些子提示单独看时无害，但组合在一起时会变得有害。现有的LLM安全基准一次评估一个提示，或在单个聊天的多个回合中评估，因此未能寻找跨会话、没有共享上下文的恶意信号。我们构建了FragBench，这是一个基于24个真实网络事件活动的基准，保留了完整的攻击轨迹：多片段杀伤链、每个片段的安全评判结果、沙箱执行痕迹，以及一组匹配的良性覆盖会话。FragBench将这一轨迹分为两个配对任务：一个对抗重写器，增强片段抵御单回合安全评判（FragBench Attack），以及一个基于图的用户级检测器，训练于结果交互（FragBench Defense）。单回合评判在发布的语料库中几乎是随机的，但四个GNN变体和三个经典机器学习基线都恢复了跨会话特征，达到聚合事件级F1 = 0.88-0.96。因此，防御碎片化的LLM误用需要建模跨会话交互图，而不是孤立的提示。我们的生成器、重写器、沙箱工具和检测器已发布在https://github.com/LidaSafety/fragbench。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the challenge of detecting cross-session attacks in language models, where malicious prompts are disguised as benign fragments. Previous methods focused on evaluating prompts individually or within a single chat session, failing to capture the malicious intent that emerges when fragments are combined across different sessions. The proposed approach, FragBench, introduces a benchmark that tracks the entire attack sequence and splits it into two tasks: an adversarial rewriter to enhance fragment safety and a graph-based detector to identify malicious interactions. The study demonstrates that existing single-turn safety judges are ineffective, while the proposed graph-based methods achieve an impressive event-level F1 score between 0.88 and 0.96, indicating that effective defense against fragmented misuse requires understanding the interactions across sessions. The contributions include a comprehensive framework for evaluating and defending against such attacks, with tools made available for further research.
本研究解决了检测恶意提示的问题，这些提示被分割成看似良性的子提示，能够逃避现有的安全基准，这些基准在孤立或单一会话中评估提示。以往的方法未能考虑跨多个会话的上下文，导致对这种跨会话攻击的检测不足。提出的方法FragBench引入了一个基准，捕获来自真实网络事件的完整攻击轨迹，并将其分为两个任务：一个对抗重写器以增强片段安全性，以及一个基于图的用户级检测器以识别恶意交互。该方法论表明，跨会话建模交互图显著提高了检测性能，事件级F1分数达到0.88至0.96，从而支持有效防御分段LLM滥用的目标。
Theoretical Limits of Language Model Alignment
Authors: Lucas Monteiro Paes, Natalie Mackraz, Barry-John Theobald, Federico Danieli
First: 2026-05-08T01:32:22+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-08T01:32:22+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Language model (LM) alignment improves model outputs to reflect human preferences while preserving the capabilities of the base model. The most common alignment approaches are (i) reinforcement learning, which maximizes the expected reward under a KL-divergence constraint, and (ii) best-of-$N$ alignment, which selects the highest-reward output among $N$ independent samples. Despite their widespread use, the fundamental limits of reward improvement under a KL budget remain poorly understood. We characterize the information-theoretic limits of KL-regularized alignment by deriving the maximum achievable expected reward gain for a fixed KL-divergence budget. Our first result provides a closed-form expression for the optimal reward improvement, governed by a Jeffreys divergence term rather than the $\sqrt{\texttt{KL}}$ used in prior analyses. We further reformulate this expression as a covariance under the base model, yielding a practical estimator that predicts achievable alignment gains from base model samples alone. We extend our analysis to the proxy reward setting, showing that the gap between ideal and proxy alignment (reward hacking) grows with the magnitude of reward error and when the KL penalty factor decreases. We then prove that reward ensembling mitigates reward hacking, providing a theoretical justification for this technique used in practice. Empirically, we compute the KL-reward Pareto frontier for two tasks for LMs, safety and summarization, and show that best-of-$N$ closely approaches the theoretical limit, while PPO and GRPO remain substantially suboptimal. Our theoretical results shed light on several empirically observed phenomena in the alignment literature and suggest that algorithmic improvements are needed to achieve optimal alignment without high inference costs.
中文标题/摘要
标题：语言模型对齐的理论极限
语言模型（LM）对齐改善模型输出，使其反映人类偏好，同时保留基础模型的能力。最常见的对齐方法是（i）强化学习，在KL散度约束下最大化期望奖励，以及（ii）最佳$N$对齐，从$N$个独立样本中选择最高奖励输出。尽管这些方法被广泛使用，但在KL预算下奖励改进的基本极限仍然不够清楚。我们通过推导固定KL散度预算下可实现的最大期望奖励增益，来表征KL正则化对齐的信息论极限。我们的第一个结果提供了最优奖励改进的封闭形式表达式，该表达式由Jeffreys散度项主导，而不是先前分析中使用的$\sqrt{\texttt{KL}}$。我们进一步将该表达式重新表述为基础模型下的协方差，得出一个实用的估计器，仅通过基础模型样本预测可实现的对齐增益。我们将分析扩展到代理奖励设置，表明理想对齐与代理对齐（奖励黑客）之间的差距随着奖励误差的大小和KL惩罚因子的降低而增加。然后我们证明奖励集成可以减轻奖励黑客，为这一实践中使用的技术提供理论依据。通过实证，我们计算了两个任务（安全性和摘要）的KL-奖励帕累托前沿，并显示最佳$N$接近理论极限，而PPO和GRPO仍然显著次优。我们的理论结果阐明了对齐文献中观察到的几个经验现象，并建议需要算法改进以在不高推理成本的情况下实现最优对齐。
Summary / 总结
This paper addresses the challenge of aligning language models (LMs) with human preferences while maintaining their capabilities, highlighting the limitations of existing methods such as reinforcement learning and best-of-$N$ alignment, which do not fully understand the fundamental limits of reward improvement under a KL-divergence constraint. When No Benchmark Exists: Validating Comparative LLM Safety Scoring Without Ground-Truth Labels
Authors: Sushant Gautam, Finn Schwall, Annika Willoch Olstad, Fernando Vallecillos Ruiz, Birk Torpmann-Hagen, Sunniva Maria Stordal Bjørklund, Leon Moonen, Klas Pettersen, Michael A. Riegler
First: 2026-05-07T17:56:41+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T17:56:41+00:00
Comments: SimpleAudit Repository: https://github.com/kelkalot/simpleaudit
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Many deployments must compare candidate language models for safety before a labeled benchmark exists for the relevant language, sector, or regulatory regime. We formalize this setting as benchmarkless comparative safety scoring and specify the contract under which a scenario-based audit can be interpreted as deployment evidence. Scores are valid only under a fixed scenario pack, rubric, auditor, judge, sampling configuration, and rerun budget. Because no labels are available, we replace ground-truth agreement with an instrumental-validity chain: responsiveness to a controlled safe-versus-abliterated contrast, dominance of target-driven variance over auditor and judge artifacts, and stability across reruns. We instantiate the chain in SimpleAudit, a local-first scoring instrument, and validate it on a Norwegian safety pack. Safe and abliterated targets separate with AUROC values between 0.89 and 1.00, target identity is the dominant variance component ($η^2 \approx 0.52$), and severity profiles stabilize by ten reruns. Applying the same chain to Petri shows that it admits both tools. The substantial differences arise upstream of the chain, in claim-contract enforcement and deployment fit. A Norwegian public-sector procurement case comparing Borealis and Gemma 3 demonstrates the resulting evidence in practice: the safer model depends on scenario category and risk measure. Consequently, scores, matched deltas, critical rates, uncertainty, and the auditor and judge used must be reported together rather than collapsed into a single ranking.

许多部署必须在相关语言、行业或监管制度的标记基准存在之前比较候选语言模型的安全性。我们将这种情况形式化为无基准的比较安全评分，并指定场景基础审计可以被解释为部署证据的合同。分数仅在固定的场景包、评分标准、审计员、评判者、抽样配置和重跑预算下有效。由于没有可用的标签，我们用一个工具有效性链替代真实一致性：对受控的安全与消除对比的响应、目标驱动方差对审计员和评判者伪影的主导性，以及重跑的稳定性。我们在SimpleAudit中实例化该链，这是一个本地优先的评分工具，并在挪威安全包上验证。安全和消除目标的AUROC值在0.89到1.00之间，目标身份是主导方差成分（$η^2 \approx 0.52$），严重性轮廓在十次重跑中稳定。将相同的链应用于Petri表明它同时接受这两种工具。显著差异出现在链的上游，在索赔合同执行和部署适配中。一个比较Borealis和Gemma 3的挪威公共部门采购案例展示了实践中的证据：更安全的模型依赖于场景类别和风险度量。因此，分数、匹配的增量、关键率、不确定性以及使用的审计员和评判者必须一起报告，而不是合并为单一排名。

This paper contributes by formalizing the scoring process and demonstrating its effectiveness with the SimpleAudit tool, validated on a Norwegian safety pack, achieving AUROC values between 0.89 and 1.00 and showing that model safety varies by scenario and risk measure. Beyond Accuracy: Policy Invariance as a Reliability Test for LLM Safety Judges
Authors: Shihao Weng, Yang Feng, Xiaofei Xie
First: 2026-05-07T12:49:09+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T12:49:09+00:00
Comments: 9 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
LLM-as-a-Judge pipelines have become the de facto evaluator for agent safety, yet existing benchmarks treat their verdicts as ground-truth proxies without checking whether the verdicts depend on the agent's behavior or merely on how the evaluation policy happens to be worded. We argue that any trustworthy safety judge must satisfy a basic property we call policy invariance, and we operationalize it as three testable principles: rubric-semantics invariance under certified-equivalent rewrites, rubric-threshold invariance under intentional strict-to-lenient shifts, and ambiguity-aware calibration so that verdict instability concentrates on genuinely ambiguous cases. Instantiating these principles as a stress-test protocol with four agent-class judges on trajectories drawn from ASSEBench and R-Judge, we surface a previously unmeasured failure mode: today's judges respond to meaningful normative shifts and to meaningless structural rewrites with comparable strength, and cannot tell the two apart. Content-preserving policy rewrites flip up to 9.1% of verdicts above baseline jitter, and 18-43% of all observed flips occur on unambiguous cases under such rewrites, so existing safety scores conflate what the agent did with how the evaluator was prompted. Beyond the diagnosis, we contribute the Policy Invariance Score and the Judge Card reporting protocol, which expose an order-of-magnitude spread in judge reliability that is invisible to accuracy-only leaderboards. We release the protocol and code so that future agent-safety benchmarks can audit their own evaluators rather than trust them by default.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越准确性：政策不变性作为LLM安全评判者的可靠性测试
LLM作为评判者的管道已成为代理安全的事实评估者，但现有基准将其裁决视为真实代理，而未检查裁决是否依赖于代理的行为或仅仅依赖于评估政策的措辞。我们认为，任何值得信赖的安全评判者必须满足我们称之为政策不变性的基本属性，并将其操作化为三个可测试的原则：在经过认证的等效重写下的评分语义不变性、在有意的严格到宽松的转变下的评分阈值不变性，以及意识到歧义的校准，以便裁决的不稳定性集中在真正模糊的案例上。将这些原则实例化为一个压力测试协议，使用来自ASSEBench和R-Judge的轨迹上的四个代理类别评判者，我们揭示了一种以前未测量的失败模式：今天的评判者对有意义的规范性变化和无意义的结构重写的反应强度相当，无法区分二者。内容保留的政策重写使得高达9.1%的裁决在基线抖动之上发生变化，18-43%的所有观察到的变化发生在此类重写下的明确案例中，因此现有的安全评分混淆了代理所做的事情与评估者的提示方式。除了诊断，我们贡献了政策不变性评分和评判者卡报告协议，揭示了评判者可靠性在仅依赖准确性排行榜中不可见的数量级差异。我们发布了该协议和代码，以便未来的代理安全基准可以审计自己的评估者，而不是默认信任他们。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the reliability of LLM-as-a-Judge pipelines used for agent safety evaluations, highlighting that existing benchmarks often treat the judges' verdicts as definitive without assessing their dependence on the evaluation policy. Previous methods fail to ensure that safety judges exhibit policy invariance, leading to potential misinterpretations of agent behavior based on how questions are framed. The proposed approach introduces three testable principles of policy invariance, operationalized through a stress-test protocol that reveals significant flaws in current judges' responses to normative shifts versus structural rewrites. The paper contributes the Policy Invariance Score and the Judge Card reporting protocol, which reveal substantial variability in judge reliability that is not captured by traditional accuracy metrics. The methodology is validated through experiments on agent-class judges using trajectories from ASSEBench and R-Judge, demonstrating that existing safety scores can misrepresent agent actions, with findings indicating up to 9.1% of verdicts being affected by content-preserving rewrites, thus supporting the need for improved evaluation standards.

XL-SafetyBench: A Country-Grounded Cross-Cultural Benchmark for LLM Safety and Cultural Sensitivity
Authors: Dasol Choi, Eugenia Kim, Jaewon Noh, Sang Seo, Eunmi Kim, Myunggyo Oh, Yunjin Park, Brigitta Jesica Kartono, Josef Pichlmeier, Helena Berndt, Sai Krishna Mendu, Glenn Johannes Tungka, Özlem Gökçe, Suresh Gehlot, Katherine Pratt, Amanda Minnich, Haon Park
First: 2026-05-07T04:35:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-07T04:35:03+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current LLM safety benchmarks are predominantly English-centric and often rely on translation, failing to capture country-specific harms. Moreover, they rarely evaluate a model's ability to detect culturally embedded sensitivities as distinct from universal harms. We introduce XL-SafetyBench. a suite of 5,500 test cases across 10 country-language pairs, comprising a Jailbreak Benchmark of country-grounded adversarial prompts and a Cultural Benchmark where local sensitivities are embedded within innocuous requests. Each item is constructed via a multi-stage pipeline that combines LLM-assisted discovery, automated validation gates, and dual independent native-speaker annotators per country. To distinguish principled refusal from comprehension failure, we evaluate Attack Success Rate (ASR) alongside two complementary metrics we introduce: Neutral-Safe Rate (NSR) and Cultural Sensitivity Rate (CSR). Evaluating 10 frontier and 27 local LLMs reveals two key findings. First, jailbreak robustness and cultural awareness do not show a coupled relationship among frontier models, so a composite safety score obscures per-axis variation. Second, local models exhibit a near-linear ASR-NSR trade-off (r = -0.81), indicating that their apparent safety reflects generation failure rather than genuine alignment. XL-SafetyBench enables more nuanced, cross-cultural safety evaluation in the multilingual era.

Safety and accuracy follow different scaling laws in clinical large language models
Authors: Sebastian Wind, Tri-Thien Nguyen, Jeta Sopa, Mahshad Lotfinia, Sebastian Bickelhaup, Michael Uder, Harald Köstler, Gerhard Wellein, Sven Nebelung, Daniel Truhn, Andreas Maier, Soroosh Tayebi Arasteh
First: 2026-05-05T17:57:19+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-05T17:57:19+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Clinical LLMs are often scaled by increasing model size, context length, retrieval complexity, or inference-time compute, with the implicit expectation that higher accuracy implies safer behavior. This assumption is incomplete in medicine, where a few confident, high-risk, or evidence-contradicting errors can matter more than average benchmark performance. We introduce SaFE-Scale, a framework for measuring how clinical LLM safety changes across model scale, evidence quality, retrieval strategy, context exposure, and inference-time compute. To instantiate this framework, we introduce RadSaFE-200, a Radiology Safety-Focused Evaluation benchmark of 200 multiple-choice questions with clinician-defined clean evidence, conflict evidence, and option-level labels for high-risk error, unsafe answer, and evidence contradiction. We evaluated 34 locally deployed LLMs across six deployment conditions: closed-book prompting (zero-shot), clean evidence, conflict evidence, standard RAG, agentic RAG, and max-context prompting. Clean evidence produced the strongest improvement, increasing mean accuracy from 73.5% to 94.1%, while reducing high-risk error from 12.0% to 2.6%, contradiction from 12.7% to 2.3%, and dangerous overconfidence from 8.0% to 1.6%. Standard RAG and agentic RAG did not reproduce this safety profile: agentic RAG improved accuracy over standard RAG and reduced contradiction, but high-risk error and dangerous overconfidence remained elevated. Max-context prompting increased latency without closing the safety gap, and additional inference-time compute produced only limited gains. Worst-case analysis showed that clinically consequential errors concentrated in a small subset of questions. Clinical LLM safety is therefore not a passive consequence of scaling, but a deployment property shaped by evidence quality, retrieval design, context construction, and collective failure behavior.
中文标题/摘要
标题：临床大型语言模型中的安全性和准确性遵循不同的缩放法则
临床LLM通常通过增加模型大小、上下文长度、检索复杂性或推理时计算来进行缩放，隐含的期望是更高的准确性意味着更安全的行为。这个假设在医学中是不完整的，因为少数自信的高风险或与证据相矛盾的错误可能比平均基准表现更重要。我们引入了SaFE-Scale，一个测量临床LLM安全性如何随模型规模、证据质量、检索策略、上下文暴露和推理时计算变化的框架。为了实现这个框架，我们引入了RadSaFE-200，这是一个以放射学安全为重点的评估基准，包含200个多项选择题，具有临床医生定义的干净证据、冲突证据和高风险错误、不安全答案及证据矛盾的选项级标签。我们在六种部署条件下评估了34个本地部署的LLM：闭卷提示（零-shot）、干净证据、冲突证据、标准RAG、代理RAG和最大上下文提示。干净证据产生了最强的改进，将平均准确性从73.5%提高到94.1%，同时将高风险错误从12.0%降低到2.6%，矛盾从12.7%降低到2.3%，危险的过度自信从8.0%降低到1.6%。标准RAG和代理RAG没有再现这种安全特征：代理RAG提高了准确性并减少了矛盾，但高风险错误和危险的过度自信仍然较高。最大上下文提示增加了延迟而没有缩小安全差距，额外的推理时计算仅产生有限的收益。最坏情况分析显示，临床相关错误集中在少数问题上。因此，临床LLM的安全性并不是缩放的被动结果，而是由证据质量、检索设计、上下文构建和集体失败行为塑造的部署属性。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the inadequacy of existing methods for scaling clinical large language models (LLMs), which often assume that increased model size and complexity will lead to improved safety and accuracy. The proposed SaFE-Scale framework offers a novel approach to measure how safety in clinical LLMs varies with different scaling factors, including model size and evidence quality. The paper introduces the RadSaFE-200 benchmark, consisting of 200 multiple-choice questions designed to evaluate high-risk errors and unsafe responses. Through testing 34 LLMs under various conditions, the study finds that using clean evidence significantly enhances accuracy and reduces high-risk errors, while other methods like standard and agentic retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) do not achieve the same safety improvements. The findings indicate that safety in clinical LLMs is influenced by multiple factors beyond mere scaling, highlighting the need for careful consideration of evidence and retrieval strategies in model deployment.
本研究解决了现有方法的不足，即假设临床大型语言模型（LLMs）中的更高准确性与更安全的行为相关，特别是在医学背景下，高风险错误可能产生重大后果。提出的SaFE-Scale框架衡量临床LLMs在模型规模和证据质量等多种因素下的安全性，并引入RadSaFE-200基准以评估以安全为重点的性能。研究在不同部署条件下评估了34个LLMs，发现使用清洁证据显著提高了准确性，从73.5%提高到94.1%，同时减少了高风险错误和矛盾。研究结果表明，临床LLMs的安全性不仅仅是规模扩展的副产品，而是受到特定部署策略和证据质量的影响，强调了增强安全性和准确性所需的定制方法。
Exposing LLM Safety Gaps Through Mathematical Encoding:New Attacks and Systematic Analysis
Authors: Haoyu Zhang, Mohammad Zandsalimy, Shanu Sushmita
First: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-05T07:25:33+00:00
Comments: 16 pages, 2 figures, 4 tables. Accepted as a long paper at the 39th Canadian Conference on Artificial Intelligence (Canadian AI 2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) employ safety mechanisms to prevent harmful outputs, yet these defenses primarily rely on semantic pattern matching. We show that encoding harmful prompts as coherent mathematical problems -- using formalisms such as set theory, formal logic, and quantum mechanics -- bypasses these filters at high rates, achieving 46%--56% average attack success across eight target models and two established benchmarks. Crucially, the effectiveness depends not on mathematical notation itself, but on whether a helper LLM deeply reformulates the harmful content into a genuine mathematical problem: rule-based encodings that apply mathematical formatting without such reformulation perform no better than unencoded baselines. We introduce a novel Formal Logic encoding that achieves attack success comparable to Set Theory, demonstrating that this vulnerability generalizes across mathematical formalisms. Additional experiments with repeat post-processing confirm that these attacks are robust to simple prompt augmentation. Notably, newer models (GPT-5, GPT-5-Mini) show substantially greater robustness than older models, though they remain vulnerable. Our findings highlight fundamental gaps in current safety frameworks and motivate defenses that reason about mathematical structure rather than surface-level semantics.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过数学编码揭示大型语言模型的安全漏洞：新攻击与系统分析
大型语言模型（LLMs）采用安全机制以防止有害输出，但这些防御主要依赖于语义模式匹配。我们展示了将有害提示编码为连贯的数学问题——使用集合论、形式逻辑和量子力学等形式化方法——可以高效绕过这些过滤器，在八个目标模型和两个已建立基准上实现46%至56%的平均攻击成功率。关键在于，效果并不依赖于数学符号本身，而在于辅助LLM是否将有害内容深度重构为真正的数学问题：应用数学格式的基于规则的编码在没有这种重构的情况下表现不佳，无法超越未编码的基线。我们引入了一种新颖的形式逻辑编码，其攻击成功率与集合论相当，表明这种脆弱性在数学形式化中具有普遍性。对重复后处理的额外实验确认这些攻击对简单提示增强具有鲁棒性。值得注意的是，较新的模型（GPT-5，GPT-5-Mini）显示出比旧模型更大的鲁棒性，尽管它们仍然脆弱。我们的发现突显了当前安全框架中的基本缺口，并激励针对数学结构而非表面语义进行推理的防御措施。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the limitations of current safety mechanisms in large language models (LLMs), which primarily rely on semantic pattern matching to prevent harmful outputs. Previous methods have struggled with encoding harmful prompts effectively, leading to vulnerabilities that can be exploited. The proposed approach introduces a novel encoding technique that reformulates harmful content into coherent mathematical problems, demonstrating that the success of these attacks is contingent on this reformulation rather than just mathematical notation. The paper contributes by revealing significant safety gaps in existing frameworks and presenting a Formal Logic encoding that achieves attack success rates of 46% to 56% across multiple models and benchmarks. The methodology includes systematic analysis and experimentation with various mathematical formalisms, confirming that even newer models remain vulnerable despite improved robustness. Overall, the findings underscore the need for enhanced defenses that focus on the mathematical structure of prompts rather than superficial semantic features.

From Prompt to Physical Actuation: Holistic Threat Modeling of LLM-Enabled Robotic Systems
Authors: Neha Nagaraja, Hayretdin Bahsi, Carlo R. da Cunha
First: 2026-04-29T23:44:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-05-04T05:54:12+00:00
Comments: Submitted to 23rd Annual International Conference on Privacy, Security, and Trust (PST2026)
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models are integrated into autonomous robotic systems for task planning and control, compromised inputs or unsafe model outputs can propagate through the planning pipeline to physical-world consequences. Although prior work has studied robotic cybersecurity, adversarial perception attacks, and LLM safety independently, no existing study traces how these threat categories interact and propagate across trust boundaries in a unified architectural model. We address this gap by modeling an LLM-enabled autonomous robot in an edge-cloud architecture as a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram and applying STRIDE-per-interaction analysis across six boundary-crossing interaction points using a three-category taxonomy of Conventional Cyber Threats, Adversarial Threats, and Conversational Threats. The analysis reveals that these categories converge at the same boundary crossings, and we trace three cross-boundary attack chains from external entry points to unsafe physical actuation, each exposing a distinct architectural property: the absence of independent semantic validation between user input and actuator dispatch, cross-modal translation from visual perception to language-model instruction, and unmediated boundary crossing through provider-side tool use. To our knowledge, this is the first DFD-based threat analysis integrating all three threat categories across the full perception-planning-actuation pipeline of an LLM-enabled robotic system.
中文标题/摘要
标题：从提示到物理执行：LLM驱动机器人系统的整体威胁建模
随着大型语言模型被集成到自主机器人系统中进行任务规划和控制，受损的输入或不安全的模型输出可能会通过规划流程传播到物理世界的后果。尽管之前的研究独立地研究了机器人网络安全、对抗性感知攻击和LLM安全，但尚无现有研究追踪这些威胁类别如何在统一的架构模型中相互作用和传播。我们通过将LLM驱动的自主机器人建模为边缘-云架构中的分层数据流图，并在六个跨边界交互点应用基于交互的STRIDE分析，使用常规网络威胁、对抗性威胁和对话威胁的三类分类法来填补这一空白。分析表明，这些类别在相同的边界交叉处汇聚，我们追踪了三条跨边界攻击链，从外部入口点到不安全的物理执行，每条链暴露出一个独特的架构特性：用户输入与执行器调度之间缺乏独立的语义验证、从视觉感知到语言模型指令的跨模态翻译，以及通过提供方工具使用的无中介边界跨越。据我们所知，这是首个基于DFD的威胁分析，整合了LLM驱动机器人系统的所有三类威胁，涵盖了完整的感知-规划-执行流程。

Previous studies have examined robotic cybersecurity, adversarial perception attacks, and LLM safety in isolation, failing to consider how these threats interact across trust boundaries. This paper proposes a unified approach by modeling an LLM-enabled robot within an edge-cloud architecture using a hierarchical Data Flow Diagram (DFD) and conducting a STRIDE-per-interaction analysis across six interaction points. The findings reveal that conventional cyber threats, adversarial threats, and conversational threats converge at these boundaries, leading to three identified attack chains that demonstrate critical architectural vulnerabilities. This work contributes a comprehensive threat analysis framework that integrates multiple threat categories throughout the perception-planning-actuation pipeline of LLM-enabled robotic systems, marking a significant advancement in understanding and mitigating risks in this domain.

Useless but Safe? Benchmarking Utility Recovery with User Intent Clarification in Multi-Turn Conversations
Authors: Mingqian Zheng, Malia Morgan, Liwei Jiang, Carolyn Rose, Maarten Sap
First: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T18:37:18+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current LLM safety alignment techniques improve model robustness against adversarial attacks, but overlook whether and how LLMs can recover helpfulness when benign users clarify their intent. We introduce CarryOnBench, the first interactive benchmark that measures whether LLMs can revise their interpretation of user intent and recover utility, while remaining safe through multi-turn conversations. Starting from 398 seemingly harmful queries with benign underlying intents, we simulate 5,970 conversations by varying user follow-up sequences, evaluating 14 models on both intent-aligned utility and safety. CarryOnBench yields 1,866 different conversation flows of 4--12 turns, totaling 23,880 model responses. We design Ben-Util, a checklist-based metric that evaluates how well each model response fulfills the user's benign information need using atomic items. At turn one, models fulfill only 10.5--37.6% of the user's benign information need. When the same query includes the benign intent upfront, models fulfill 25.1--72.1%, confirming that models withhold information due to intent misinterpretation, not limited knowledge. With benign clarifications in multi-turn conversations, 13 of 14 models approach or exceed this single-turn baseline, yet recovery cost varies across models. We identify three failure modes invisible to single-turn evaluations: utility lock-in, where a model rarely updates despite clarification; unsafe recovery, where a model updates at disproportionate safety cost; and repetitive recovery, where a model recycles prior responses rather than providing new information. Moreover, conversations converge to similar harmfulness levels regardless of how conservative the model starts. These findings expose a gap that single-turn evaluations miss -- whether a model is appropriately cautious or simply unresponsive to clarified user intent.
中文标题/摘要
标题：无用但安全？在多轮对话中通过用户意图澄清基准测试实用性恢复
当前的LLM安全对齐技术提高了模型对抗攻击的鲁棒性，但忽视了LLM在良性用户澄清意图时是否以及如何恢复有用性。我们引入CarryOnBench，这是第一个交互式基准，测量LLM是否能够修正对用户意图的解释并恢复实用性，同时在多轮对话中保持安全。从398个看似有害的查询开始，这些查询具有良性的潜在意图，我们通过变化用户后续序列模拟了5,970个对话，评估了14个模型在意图对齐的实用性和安全性方面的表现。CarryOnBench产生了1,866种不同的对话流程，轮次为4到12，总计23,880个模型响应。我们设计了Ben-Util，这是一个基于清单的指标，评估每个模型响应在多大程度上满足用户的良性信息需求。在第一轮中，模型仅满足用户良性信息需求的10.5%到37.6%。当同一查询在前面包含良性意图时，模型满足25.1%到72.1%，确认模型因意图误解而隐瞒信息，而不是知识有限。在多轮对话中，经过良性澄清，14个模型中有13个接近或超过这一单轮基准，但恢复成本在模型之间有所不同。我们识别出三种在单轮评估中不可见的失败模式：实用性锁定，即模型在澄清后很少更新；不安全恢复，即模型以不成比例的安全成本进行更新；以及重复恢复，即模型回收先前的响应而不是提供新信息。此外，无论模型起始时多么保守，对话都趋向于相似的有害性水平。这些发现揭示了单轮评估所忽视的一个差距——模型是否适当地谨慎，或仅仅对澄清的用户意图无反应。
Summary / 总结
This research addresses the limitations of existing large language model (LLM) safety alignment techniques, which focus on robustness against adversarial attacks but fail to assess the models' ability to recover helpfulness when users clarify their intent in multi-turn conversations. Previous methods primarily evaluated single-turn interactions, neglecting the dynamics of ongoing conversations, leading to issues such as intent misinterpretation and inadequate information fulfillment. The proposed approach, CarryOnBench, introduces an interactive benchmark that simulates 5,970 conversations to evaluate 14 models on their ability to revise interpretations and recover utility while maintaining safety. The study reveals that models initially fulfill only a fraction of benign user needs, but with clarifications, many models improve their performance, although recovery varies significantly. Key contributions include identifying failure modes that single-turn evaluations overlook and demonstrating that conversation dynamics can lead to similar harmfulness levels regardless of initial model conservativeness.

Policy-Grounded Safety Evaluation of 20 Large Language Models
Authors: Juan Manuel Contreras
First: 2025-07-19T18:49:16+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-29T15:54:46+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly integrated into real-world applications, scalable and rigorous safety evaluation is essential. This paper introduces Aymara AI, a programmatic platform for generating and administering customized, policy-grounded safety evaluations. Aymara AI transforms natural-language safety policies into adversarial prompts and scores model responses using an AI-based rater validated against human judgments. We demonstrate its capabilities through the Aymara LLM Risk and Responsibility Matrix, which evaluates 20 commercially available LLMs across 10 real-world safety domains. Results reveal wide performance disparities, with mean safety scores ranging from 86.2% to 52.4%. While models performed well in well-established safety domains such as Misinformation (mean = 95.7%), they consistently failed in more complex or underspecified domains, notably Privacy & Impersonation (mean = 24.3%). Analyses of Variance confirmed that safety scores differed significantly across both models and domains (p < .05). These findings underscore the inconsistent and context-dependent nature of LLM safety and highlight the need for scalable, customizable tools like Aymara AI to support responsible AI development and oversight.
中文标题/摘要
标题：基于政策的20个大型语言模型的安全评估
随着大型语言模型（LLMs）越来越多地融入现实应用，规模化和严格的安全评估变得至关重要。本文介绍了Aymara AI，一个用于生成和管理定制化、基于政策的安全评估的程序化平台。Aymara AI将自然语言安全政策转化为对抗性提示，并使用经过人类判断验证的基于AI的评分者对模型响应进行评分。我们通过Aymara LLM风险与责任矩阵展示其能力，该矩阵评估了20个商业可用的LLM在10个现实安全领域的表现。结果显示，性能差异显著，平均安全评分范围从86.2%到52.4%。虽然模型在虚假信息等成熟安全领域表现良好（平均 = 95.7%），但在更复杂或不明确的领域（特别是隐私与冒充）中表现不佳（平均 = 24.3%）。方差分析确认，安全评分在模型和领域之间存在显著差异（p < .05）。这些发现强调了LLM安全性的不一致性和依赖于上下文的特性，并突显了像Aymara AI这样的可扩展、可定制工具在支持负责任的AI开发和监督中的必要性。

Evaluating LLM Safety Under Repeated Inference via Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing
Authors: Keita Broadwater
First: 2026-02-12T10:09:13+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-28T16:38:37+00:00
Comments: 23 pages, 9 figures; editorial and LaTeX revisions for clarity; improved presentation of methodology and results; updated figures, tables, and float placement; clarified temperature sensitivity and deployment-risk analysis; expanded reporting from the same experiments; results unchanged in substance
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Traditional benchmarks for large language models (LLMs), such as HELM and AIR-BENCH, primarily assess safety through breadth-oriented evaluation across diverse tasks and risk categories. However, real-world deployment often exposes a different class of risk: operational failures that arise under repeated inference on identical or near-identical prompts rather than from broad task-level underperformance. In high-stakes settings, response consistency and safety under sustained use are therefore critical. We introduce Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST), a depth-oriented evaluation framework inspired by highly accelerated stress testing in reliability engineering. APST repeatedly samples identical prompts under controlled operational conditions (such as decoding temperature) to surface latent failure modes including hallucinations, refusal inconsistency, and unsafe completions. Rather than treating failures as isolated events, APST models them as stochastic outcomes of repeated inference and uses Bernoulli and binomial formulations to estimate per-inference failure probabilities. Applying APST to multiple instruction-tuned LLMs evaluated on AIR-BENCH 2024--derived safety and security prompts, we find that models with comparable shallow-evaluation scores can exhibit substantially different empirical failure rates under repeated sampling. These results show that single-sample or low-depth evaluation can obscure meaningful differences in deployment-relevant reliability. APST complements existing benchmark methodologies by providing a practical framework for estimating failure frequency under sustained use and comparing safety reliability across models and decoding configurations.
中文标题/摘要
标题：通过加速提示压力测试评估大语言模型的安全性
传统的大语言模型（LLMs）基准，如HELM和AIR-BENCH，主要通过在多样任务和风险类别中的广度评估来评估安全性。然而，实际部署往往暴露出另一类风险：在相同或近似相同提示下重复推理所导致的操作失败，而不是广泛任务级别的表现不佳。在高风险环境中，响应一致性和持续使用下的安全性至关重要。我们引入了加速提示压力测试（APST），这是一种受可靠性工程中高度加速压力测试启发的深度评估框架。APST在受控操作条件下（如解码温度）重复采样相同的提示，以揭示潜在的失败模式，包括幻觉、拒绝不一致和不安全的完成。APST将失败视为重复推理的随机结果，并使用伯努利和二项式公式来估计每次推理的失败概率。将APST应用于多个在AIR-BENCH 2024上评估的指令调优LLMs的安全和安全提示，我们发现具有可比浅层评估分数的模型在重复采样下可能表现出显著不同的经验失败率。这些结果表明，单样本或低深度评估可能掩盖在部署相关可靠性方面的有意义差异。APST通过提供一个实用框架来估计持续使用下的失败频率，并比较模型和解码配置之间的安全可靠性，补充了现有的基准方法。
Summary / 总结
This article addresses the limitations of traditional benchmarks for evaluating large language models (LLMs), which primarily focus on broad task performance and often overlook operational failures that occur during repeated inference on similar prompts. Existing methods fail to capture the nuances of response consistency and safety in high-stakes environments, prompting the authors to propose Accelerated Prompt Stress Testing (APST), a depth-oriented evaluation framework that simulates repeated sampling of identical prompts under controlled conditions. APST models failures as stochastic outcomes and employs Bernoulli and binomial formulations to estimate failure probabilities, revealing significant differences in empirical failure rates among models that appear similar in shallow evaluations. The methodology demonstrates that APST effectively identifies latent failure modes and enhances the understanding of model reliability in real-world applications, thus contributing a practical tool for assessing LLM safety under sustained use.
本文探讨了传统的大型语言模型（LLMs）评估基准的局限性，这些基准通常侧重于在各种任务和风险类别中的广度评估，而忽视了在相似提示下重复推理时可能发生的操作失败。现有方法未能捕捉高风险环境中响应一致性和安全性的细微差别，因此作者提出了加速提示压力测试（APST），这是一种深度评估框架，通过在受控条件下对相同提示进行重复采样来识别潜在的失败模式。该研究的贡献在于能够将失败建模为随机结果，并使用伯努利和二项式公式估计失败概率，揭示了具有相似浅层评估分数的模型在实际应用中可能具有显著不同的失败率。通过将APST应用于多个指令调优的LLMs，研究表明传统的低深度评估可能掩盖可靠性的重要差异，从而提供了一种更有效的框架来评估模型和配置的安全性和可靠性。
Adaptive Prompt Embedding Optimization for LLM Jailbreaking
Authors: Miles Q. Li, Benjamin C. M. Fung, Boyang Li, Radin Hamidi Rad, Ebrahim Bagheri
First: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-27T20:39:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Existing white-box jailbreak attacks against aligned LLMs typically append discrete adversarial suffixes to the user prompt, which visibly alters the prompt and operates in a combinatorial token space. Prior work has avoided directly optimizing the embeddings of the original prompt tokens, presumably because perturbing them risks destroying the prompt's semantic content. We propose Prompt Embedding Optimization (PEO), a multi-round white-box jailbreak that directly optimizes the embeddings of the original prompt tokens without appending any adversarial tokens, and show that the concern is unfounded: the optimized embeddings remain close enough to their originals that the visible prompt string is preserved exactly after nearest-token projection, and quantitative analysis shows the model's responses stay on topic for the large majority of prompts. PEO combines continuous embedding-space optimization with structured continuation targets and an adaptive failure-focused schedule. Counterintuitively, later PEO rounds can benefit from heuristic composite response scaffolds that are not natural standalone templates, yet ASR-Judge shows that the resulting gains are not merely empty formatting or scaffold-only outputs. Across two standard harmful-behavior benchmarks and competing white-box attacks spanning discrete suffix search, appended adversarial embeddings, and search-based adversarial generation, PEO outperforms all of them in our experiments.
中文标题/摘要
标题：用于大型语言模型越狱的自适应提示嵌入优化
现有针对对齐大型语言模型的白盒越狱攻击通常在用户提示后附加离散的对抗后缀，这明显改变了提示并在组合标记空间中操作。之前的工作避免直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，可能是因为扰动它们会破坏提示的语义内容。我们提出了提示嵌入优化（PEO），这是一种多轮白盒越狱，直接优化原始提示标记的嵌入，而不附加任何对抗标记，并表明这种担忧是没有根据的：优化后的嵌入与原始嵌入保持足够接近，以至于在最近标记投影后可见的提示字符串完全保留，定量分析显示模型的响应在绝大多数提示中保持主题一致。PEO结合了连续嵌入空间优化、结构化延续目标和自适应失败聚焦调度。反直觉的是，后续PEO轮次可以受益于并非自然独立模板的启发式复合响应支架，但ASR-Judge显示，所获得的收益不仅仅是空格式或仅支架输出。在两个标准有害行为基准和涵盖离散后缀搜索、附加对抗嵌入和基于搜索的对抗生成的竞争白盒攻击中，PEO在我们的实验中表现优于所有这些方法。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of existing white-box jailbreak attacks on aligned large language models (LLMs), which typically modify user prompts by appending adversarial suffixes, leading to visible alterations and operating within a combinatorial token space. Previous methods have avoided optimizing the original prompt embeddings due to concerns about losing semantic integrity, but this paper introduces Prompt Embedding Optimization (PEO), a novel approach that directly optimizes these embeddings without adding adversarial tokens, demonstrating that the semantic content can be preserved. The contribution of this work lies in its multi-round optimization strategy that combines continuous embedding-space optimization with structured continuation targets and an adaptive failure-focused schedule, showing significant improvements over traditional methods. The methodology was tested against two standard harmful-behavior benchmarks and various competing white-box attacks, with PEO achieving superior performance, thus supporting its effectiveness in maintaining prompt integrity while enhancing jailbreak capabilities.

Beyond Context: Large Language Models' Failure to Grasp Users' Intent
Authors: Ahmed M. Hussain, Salahuddin Salahuddin
First: 2025-12-24T11:15:57+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T20:27:34+00:00
Comments: 22 pages and 23 figures; updated authors list and revised manuscript
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Current Large Language Models (LLMs) safety approaches focus on explicitly harmful content while overlooking a critical vulnerability: the inability to understand context and recognize user intent. This creates exploitable vulnerabilities that malicious users can systematically leverage to circumvent safety mechanisms. We empirically evaluate multiple state-of-the-art LLMs, including ChatGPT, Claude, Gemini, and DeepSeek. Our analysis demonstrates the circumvention of reliable safety mechanisms through emotional framing, progressive revelation, and academic justification techniques. Notably, reasoning-enabled configurations amplified rather than mitigated the effectiveness of exploitation, increasing factual precision while failing to interrogate the underlying intent. The exception was Claude Opus 4.1, which prioritized intent detection over information provision in some use cases. This pattern reveals that current architectural designs create systematic vulnerabilities. These limitations require paradigmatic shifts toward contextual understanding and intent recognition as core safety capabilities rather than post-hoc protective mechanisms.
中文标题/摘要
标题：超越上下文：大型语言模型未能理解用户意图
当前大型语言模型（LLMs）的安全方法专注于显性有害内容，而忽视了一个关键漏洞：无法理解上下文和识别用户意图。这导致了恶意用户可以系统性利用的可利用漏洞，从而规避安全机制。我们对多个最先进的LLMs进行了实证评估，包括ChatGPT、Claude、Gemini和DeepSeek。我们的分析表明，通过情感框架、渐进揭示和学术辩护技术，可靠安全机制被规避。值得注意的是，启用推理的配置增强了而不是减轻了利用的有效性，提高了事实精确性，但未能质疑潜在意图。例外是Claude Opus 4.1，在某些用例中优先考虑意图检测而非信息提供。这一模式揭示了当前架构设计造成的系统性漏洞。这些局限性需要在上下文理解和意图识别方面进行范式转变，将其作为核心安全能力，而不是事后保护机制。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses a significant gap in the safety mechanisms of Large Language Models (LLMs), which primarily focus on harmful content but fail to understand user intent and context, leading to exploitable vulnerabilities. Previous methods inadequately addressed these issues, allowing malicious users to bypass safety features through techniques like emotional framing and progressive revelation. This paper proposes a shift in focus towards integrating contextual understanding and intent recognition as fundamental safety capabilities, rather than relying on reactive measures. The methodology involves empirical evaluation of several leading LLMs, revealing that while most models, including ChatGPT and Gemini, struggle with intent recognition, Claude Opus 4.1 shows promise by prioritizing intent detection in specific scenarios. The findings indicate that current LLM architectures create systematic vulnerabilities, necessitating a rethinking of safety approaches to enhance user intent comprehension and context awareness.

Logic Jailbreak: Efficiently Unlocking LLM Safety Restrictions Through Formal Logical Expression
Authors: Jingyu Peng, Maolin Wang, Nan Wang, Jiatong Li, Yuchen Li, Yuyang Ye, Wanyu Wang, Pengyue Jia, Kai Zhang, Xiangyu Zhao
First: 2025-05-18T04:23:51+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T07:04:26+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Despite substantial advancements in aligning large language models (LLMs) with human values, current safety mechanisms remain susceptible to jailbreak attacks. We hypothesize that this vulnerability stems from distributional discrepancies between alignment-oriented prompts and malicious prompts. To investigate this, we introduce LogiBreak, a novel and universal black-box jailbreak method that leverages logical expression translation to circumvent LLM safety systems. By converting harmful natural language prompts into formal logical expressions, LogiBreak exploits the distributional gap between alignment data and logic-based inputs, preserving the underlying semantic intent and readability while evading safety constraints. We evaluate LogiBreak on a multilingual jailbreak dataset spanning three languages, demonstrating its effectiveness across various evaluation settings and linguistic contexts.
中文标题/摘要
标题：逻辑越狱：通过形式逻辑表达高效解锁大型语言模型安全限制
尽管在将大型语言模型（LLMs）与人类价值观对齐方面取得了重大进展，但当前的安全机制仍然容易受到越狱攻击。我们假设这种脆弱性源于对齐导向提示与恶意提示之间的分布差异。为此，我们引入了LogiBreak，这是一种新颖且通用的黑箱越狱方法，利用逻辑表达翻译来规避LLM安全系统。通过将有害的自然语言提示转换为形式逻辑表达，LogiBreak利用对齐数据与基于逻辑的输入之间的分布差距，保持潜在的语义意图和可读性，同时规避安全约束。我们在涵盖三种语言的多语言越狱数据集上评估LogiBreak，展示了其在各种评估设置和语言环境中的有效性。

This method is well-motivated as it directly targets the identified vulnerabilities in existing safety systems. The paper contributes by demonstrating LogiBreak's effectiveness on a multilingual jailbreak dataset across three languages, achieving significant performance improvements that support its goals of circumventing LLM safety restrictions.

Toward Principled LLM Safety Testing: Solving the Jailbreak Oracle Problem
Authors: Shuyi Lin, Anshuman Suri, Alina Oprea, Cheng Tan
First: 2025-06-17T20:37:29+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-24T04:36:54+00:00
Comments: Accepted to MLSys 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
As large language models (LLMs) become increasingly deployed in safety-critical applications, the lack of systematic methods to assess their vulnerability to jailbreak attacks presents a critical security gap. We introduce the jailbreak oracle problem: given a model, prompt, and decoding strategy, determine whether a jailbreak response can be generated with likelihood exceeding a specified threshold. This formalization enables a principled study of jailbreak vulnerabilities. Answering the jailbreak oracle problem poses significant computational challenges, as the search space grows exponentially with response length. We present Boa, the first system designed for efficiently solving the jailbreak oracle problem. Boa employs a two-phase search strategy: (1) breadth-first sampling to identify easily accessible jailbreaks, followed by (2) depth-first priority search guided by fine-grained safety scores to systematically explore promising yet low-probability paths. Boa enables rigorous security assessments including systematic defense evaluation, standardized comparison of red team attacks, and model certification under extreme adversarial conditions. Code is available at https://github.com/shuyilinn/BOA/tree/mlsys2026ae
中文标题/摘要
标题：朝着原则性的大型语言模型安全测试：解决越狱预言机问题
随着大型语言模型（LLMs）在安全关键应用中的日益部署，缺乏系统的方法来评估它们对越狱攻击的脆弱性，形成了一个关键的安全漏洞。我们引入了越狱预言机问题：给定一个模型、提示和解码策略，确定是否可以生成超过指定阈值的越狱响应。这个形式化使得对越狱脆弱性的原则性研究成为可能。回答越狱预言机问题面临显著的计算挑战，因为搜索空间随着响应长度的增加而呈指数增长。我们提出了Boa，这是第一个旨在高效解决越狱预言机问题的系统。Boa采用两阶段搜索策略：（1）广度优先采样以识别易于访问的越狱，随后（2）深度优先优先搜索，通过细粒度安全评分引导系统地探索有前景但概率较低的路径。Boa使得严格的安全评估成为可能，包括系统的防御评估、红队攻击的标准化比较，以及在极端对抗条件下的模型认证。代码可在 https://github.com/shuyilinn/BOA/tree/mlsys2026ae 获取。

Previous methods lacked systematic approaches to evaluate these vulnerabilities, leading to significant challenges in determining the likelihood of jailbreak responses. The proposed method, Boa, differs by introducing a formalized jailbreak oracle problem and employing a two-phase search strategy that combines breadth-first sampling and depth-first priority search, effectively addressing the computational challenges of the search space. AISafetyBenchExplorer: A Metric-Aware Catalogue of AI Safety Benchmarks Reveals Fragmented Measurement and Weak Benchmark Governance
Authors: Abiodun A. Solanke
First: 2026-04-14T15:26:03+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T13:27:05+00:00
Comments: This paper has been withdrawn by the author while an institutional affiliation compliance matter is under review. It may be resubmitted once the matter is resolved
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
The rapid expansion of large language model (LLM) safety evaluation has produced a substantial benchmark ecosystem, but not a correspondingly coherent measurement ecosystem. We present AISafetyBenchExplorer, a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks released between 2018 and 2026, organized through a multi-sheet schema that records benchmark-level metadata, metric-level definitions, benchmark-paper metadata, and repository activity. This design enables meta-analysis not only of what benchmarks exist, but also of how safety is operationalized, aggregated, and judged across the literature. Using the updated catalogue, we identify a central structural problem: benchmark proliferation has outpaced measurement standardization. The current landscape is dominated by medium-complexity benchmarks (94/195), while only 7 benchmarks occupy the Popular tier. The workbook further reports strong concentration around English-only evaluation (165/195), evaluation-only resources (170/195), stale GitHub repositories (137/195), stale Hugging Face datasets (96/195), and heavy reliance on arXiv preprints among benchmarks with known venue metadata. At the metric level, the catalogue shows that familiar labels such as accuracy, F1 score, safety score, and aggregate benchmark scores often conceal materially different judges, aggregation rules, and threat models. We argue that the field's main failure mode is fragmentation rather than scarcity. Researchers now have many benchmark artifacts, but they often lack a shared measurement language, a principled basis for benchmark selection, and durable stewardship norms for post publication maintenance. AISafetyBenchExplorer addresses this gap by providing a traceable benchmark catalogue, a controlled metadata schema, and a complexity taxonomy that together support more rigorous benchmark discovery, comparison, and meta-evaluation.
中文标题/摘要
标题：AISafetyBenchExplorer：一个关注指标的AI安全基准目录揭示了测量的碎片化和基准治理的薄弱
大型语言模型（LLM）安全评估的快速扩展产生了一个庞大的基准生态系统，但没有相应连贯的测量生态系统。我们提出了AISafetyBenchExplorer，这是一个结构化的目录，包含2018年至2026年间发布的195个AI安全基准，采用多表格模式记录基准级元数据、指标级定义、基准论文元数据和存储库活动。该设计不仅支持对现有基准的元分析，还支持对安全如何在文献中被操作、聚合和评判的分析。使用更新的目录，我们识别出一个核心结构性问题：基准的激增超过了测量的标准化。目前的格局以中等复杂度的基准为主（94/195），而只有7个基准位于流行层级。工作簿进一步报告了对仅英语评估（165/195）、仅评估资源（170/195）、过时的GitHub存储库（137/195）、过时的Hugging Face数据集（96/195）以及在已知场地元数据的基准中对arXiv预印本的高度依赖的强烈集中。在指标层面，目录显示，熟悉的标签如准确率、F1分数、安全分数和综合基准分数常常掩盖了实质上不同的评判者、聚合规则和威胁模型。我们认为，该领域的主要失败模式是碎片化而非稀缺。研究人员现在拥有许多基准文献，但通常缺乏共享的测量语言、基准选择的原则基础以及发布后维护的持久管理规范。AISafetyBenchExplorer通过提供可追溯的基准目录、受控的元数据模式和复杂性分类法来填补这一空白，从而支持更严格的基准发现、比较和元评估。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the fragmented landscape of AI safety benchmarks that has emerged alongside the rapid growth of large language model safety evaluations. Previous methods have resulted in a proliferation of benchmarks without a coherent measurement framework, leading to inconsistencies in how safety is assessed and reported. The proposed AISafetyBenchExplorer offers a structured catalogue of 195 AI safety benchmarks, organized with detailed metadata and a complexity taxonomy, which facilitates better benchmark discovery and comparison. This approach is well-motivated as it aims to standardize measurement practices and improve governance in the benchmark ecosystem. The methodology includes a multi-sheet schema that captures benchmark-level and metric-level information, revealing critical insights such as the dominance of medium-complexity benchmarks and the concentration of English-only evaluations. The findings highlight the need for a shared measurement language and principled benchmark selection, ultimately supporting more rigorous evaluations in AI safety research.
本研究针对随着大型语言模型安全评估的快速增长而出现的AI安全基准的碎片化现象。以往的方法导致基准的激增，但缺乏一致的测量框架，造成了标准化不足和对英语评估的高度依赖等问题。提出的AISafetyBenchExplorer提供了一个结构化的195个AI安全基准的目录，通过多表格架构捕捉详细的元数据，并支持基准特征和测量实践的元分析。这种方法是合理的，因为它旨在统一碎片化的测量生态系统，提供可追溯的基准目录和复杂性分类法，从而促进更好的基准发现和比较。该方法论允许全面概述现有基准，并强调该领域在治理和标准化方面的改进需求，最终支持对AI安全的更严格评估。
Secure LLM Fine-Tuning via Safety-Aware Probing
Authors: Chengcan Wu, Zhixin Zhang, Zeming Wei, Yihao Zhang, Xiaokun Luan, Meng Sun
First: 2025-05-22T14:52:10+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T08:31:23+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) have achieved remarkable success across many applications, but their ability to generate harmful content raises serious safety concerns. Although safety alignment techniques are often applied during pre-training or post-training, recent studies show that subsequent fine-tuning on adversarial or even benign data can still compromise model safety. In this paper, we revisit the fundamental question of why fine-tuning on non-harmful data may nevertheless degrade safety. We show that the safety and task-performance loss landscapes are partially decoupled, so updates that improve task-specific performance may still move the model toward unsafe regions. Based on this insight, we propose a safety-aware probing (SAP) optimization framework for mitigating safety risks during fine-tuning. Concretely, SAP uses contrastive safety signals to locate safety-correlated directions, and optimizes a lightweight probe that perturbs hidden-state propagation during fine-tuning, thereby steering parameter updates away from harmful trajectories while preserving task-specific learning. Extensive experiments show that SAP consistently improves the safety--utility tradeoff across multiple models and tasks. Averaged over multiple LLMs, SAP reduces the harmful score significantly relative to standard fine-tuning, outperforming strong baselines while maintaining competitive task-specific performance. SAP also demonstrates stronger robustness under harmful data poisoning, adversarial fine-tuning, and a dedicated post-fine-tuning adaptive attack, validating that SAP is an effective and scalable framework for preserving LLM safety during fine-tuning. Our code is available at https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP.

大型语言模型（LLMs）在许多应用中取得了显著成功，但其生成有害内容的能力引发了严重的安全担忧。尽管安全对齐技术通常在预训练或后训练期间应用，但最近的研究表明，随后在对抗性或甚至良性数据上的微调仍然可能危及模型安全。本文重新审视了一个基本问题，即为什么在无害数据上的微调仍可能降低安全性。我们表明，安全性和任务性能损失的景观部分解耦，因此改善任务特定性能的更新可能仍会将模型推向不安全区域。基于这一见解，我们提出了一种安全感知探测（SAP）优化框架，以减轻微调过程中的安全风险。具体而言，SAP使用对比安全信号来定位与安全相关的方向，并优化一个轻量级探测器，在微调过程中扰动隐藏状态传播，从而将参数更新引导远离有害轨迹，同时保持任务特定学习。大量实验表明，SAP在多个模型和任务中始终改善安全性与效用的权衡。在多个LLM上平均，SAP相对于标准微调显著降低了有害评分，超越了强基线，同时保持了竞争性的任务特定性能。SAP在有害数据中毒、对抗性微调和专门的后微调自适应攻击下也表现出更强的鲁棒性，验证了SAP是一个有效且可扩展的框架，用于在微调过程中保持LLM的安全性。我们的代码可在https://github.com/ChengcanWu/SAP获取。

LASA: Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment at the Semantic Bottleneck for LLM Safety
Authors: Junxiao Yang, Haoran Liu, Jinzhe Tu, Jiale Cheng, Zhexin Zhang, Shiyao Cui, Jiaqi Weng, Jialing Tao, Hui Xue, Hongning Wang, Han Qiu, Minlie Huang
First: 2026-04-13T15:59:50+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-23T04:47:08+00:00
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large language models (LLMs) often demonstrate strong safety performance in high-resource languages, yet exhibit severe vulnerabilities when queried in low-resource languages. We attribute this gap to a mismatch between language-agnostic semantic understanding ability and language-dominant safety alignment biased toward high-resource languages. Consistent with this hypothesis, we empirically identify the semantic bottleneck in LLMs, an intermediate layer in which the geometry of model representations is governed primarily by shared semantic content rather than language identity. Building on this observation, we propose Language-Agnostic Semantic Alignment (LASA), which anchors safety alignment directly in semantic bottlenecks. Experiments show that LASA substantially improves safety across all languages: average attack success rate (ASR) drops from 24.7% to 2.8% on LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct and remains around 3-4% across Qwen2.5 and Qwen3 Instruct models (7B-32B). Together, our analysis and method offer a representation-level perspective on LLM safety, suggesting that safety alignment requires anchoring safety understanding not in surface text, but in the model's language-agnostic semantic space.
中文标题/摘要
标题：LASA：在语义瓶颈处实现语言无关的语义对齐以提高大型语言模型的安全性
大型语言模型（LLMs）在高资源语言中通常表现出强大的安全性能，但在低资源语言中查询时却表现出严重的脆弱性。我们将这一差距归因于语言无关的语义理解能力与偏向高资源语言的语言主导安全对齐之间的不匹配。与这一假设一致，我们实证识别了LLMs中的语义瓶颈，这是一个中间层，其中模型表示的几何形状主要由共享的语义内容而非语言身份所主导。基于这一观察，我们提出了语言无关的语义对齐（LASA），直接在语义瓶颈中锚定安全对齐。实验表明，LASA显著提高了所有语言的安全性：在LLaMA-3.1-8B-Instruct上，平均攻击成功率（ASR）从24.7%降至2.8%，在Qwen2.5和Qwen3 Instruct模型（7B-32B）中保持在3-4%左右。我们的分析和方法共同提供了对LLM安全性的表示层面视角，表明安全对齐需要将安全理解锚定在模型的语言无关语义空间中，而非表面文本上。

Dialect vs Demographics: Quantifying LLM Bias from Implicit Linguistic Signals vs. Explicit User Profiles
Authors: Irti Haq, Belén Saldías
First: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-22T23:33:18+00:00
Comments: In The 2026 ACM Conference on Fairness, Accountability, and Transparency (FAccT '26), June 25--28, 2026, Montreal, Canada. ACM, New York, NY, USA, 32 pages
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
As state-of-the-art Large Language Models (LLMs) have become ubiquitous, ensuring equitable performance across diverse demographics is critical. However, it remains unclear whether these disparities arise from the explicitly stated identity itself or from the way identity is signaled. In real-world interactions, users' identity is often conveyed implicitly through a complex combination of various socio-linguistic factors. This study disentangles these signals by employing a factorial design with over 24,000 responses from two open-weight LLMs (Gemma-3-12B and Qwen-3-VL-8B), comparing prompts with explicitly announced user profiles against implicit dialect signals (e.g., AAVE, Singlish) across various sensitive domains. Our results uncover a unique paradox in LLM safety where users achieve ``better'' performance by sounding like a demographic than by stating they belong to it. Explicit identity prompts activate aggressive safety filters, increasing refusal rates and reducing semantic similarity compared to our reference text for Black users. In contrast, implicit dialect cues trigger a powerful ``dialect jailbreak,'' reducing refusal probability to near zero while simultaneously achieving a greater level of semantic similarity to the reference texts compared to Standard American English prompts. However, this ``dialect jailbreak'' introduces a critical safety trade-off regarding content sanitization. We find that current safety alignment techniques are brittle and over-indexed on explicit keywords, creating a bifurcated user experience where ``standard'' users receive cautious, sanitized information while dialect speakers navigate a less sanitized, more raw, and potentially a more hostile information landscape and highlights a fundamental tension in alignment--between equitable and linguistic diversity--and underscores the need for safety mechanisms that generalize beyond explicit cues.

随着最先进的大型语言模型（LLMs）变得无处不在，确保在不同人口统计中公平的表现至关重要。然而，这些差异是否源于明确声明的身份本身，还是身份信号的方式仍不清楚。在现实世界的互动中，用户的身份通常通过各种社会语言因素的复杂组合隐性传达。本研究通过采用因子设计，分析来自两个开放权重LLM（Gemma-3-12B和Qwen-3-VL-8B）的超过24,000个响应，比较显性用户档案的提示与隐性方言信号（例如，AAVE，Singlish）在各种敏感领域的表现。我们的结果揭示了LLM安全性中的一个独特悖论，即用户通过听起来像某个群体而不是明确声明自己属于该群体来获得“更好”的表现。显性身份提示激活了激进的安全过滤器，增加了拒绝率，并减少了与黑人用户参考文本的语义相似性。相比之下，隐性方言线索触发了强大的“方言越狱”，将拒绝概率降低到接近零，同时在与标准美式英语提示相比时，达到更高的语义相似性。然而，这种“方言越狱”引入了关于内容净化的关键安全权衡。我们发现当前的安全对齐技术脆弱，并过度依赖显性关键词，造成了“标准”用户获得谨慎、净化的信息，而方言使用者则在一个较少净化、更原始且可能更具敌意的信息环境中导航，突显了对齐中的基本紧张关系——在公平性与语言多样性之间，并强调了需要超越显性线索的安全机制。

LLM Safety From Within: Detecting Harmful Content with Internal Representations
Authors: Difan Jiao, Yilun Liu, Ye Yuan, Zhenwei Tang, Linfeng Du, Haolun Wu, Ashton Anderson
First: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00 · Latest: 2026-04-20T17:17:07+00:00
Comments: 17 pages,10 figures,6 tables
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Guard models are widely used to detect harmful content in user prompts and LLM responses. However, state-of-the-art guard models rely solely on terminal-layer representations and overlook the rich safety-relevant features distributed across internal layers. We present SIREN, a lightweight guard model that harnesses these internal features. By identifying safety neurons via linear probing and combining them through an adaptive layer-weighted strategy, SIREN builds a harmfulness detector from LLM internals without modifying the underlying model. Our comprehensive evaluation shows that SIREN substantially outperforms state-of-the-art open-source guard models across multiple benchmarks while using 250 times fewer trainable parameters. Moreover, SIREN exhibits superior generalization to unseen benchmarks, naturally enables real-time streaming detection, and significantly improves inference efficiency compared to generative guard models. Overall, our results highlight LLM internal states as a promising foundation for practical, high-performance harmfulness detection.
